# Kubernetes Controller Runtime Reconciler Registration

## Your Task

Trace how a controller registers itself with the controller-runtime Manager in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find the Go source files that define the Reconciler interface, implement SetupWithManager, and wire the controller into the manager's reconcile loop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

   495→func NewControllerDescriptors() map[string]*ControllerDescriptor {
   496→	controllers := map[string]*ControllerDescriptor{}
   497→	aliases := sets.NewString()
   498→
   499→	// All the controllers must fulfil common constraints, or else we will explode.
   500→	register := func(controllerDesc *ControllerDescriptor) {
   501→		if controllerDesc == nil {
   502→			panic("received nil controller for a registration")
   503→		}
   504→		name := controllerDesc.Name()
   505→		if len(name) == 0 {
   506→			panic("received controller without a name for a registration")
   507→		}
   508→		if _, found := controllers[name]; found {
   509→			panic(fmt.Sprintf("controller name %q was registered twice", name))
   510→		}
   511→		if controllerDesc.GetInitFunc() == nil {
   512→			panic(fmt.Sprintf("controller %q does not have an init function", name))
   513→		}
   514→
   515→		for _, alias := range controllerDesc.GetAliases() {
   516→			if aliases.Has(alias) {
   517→				panic(fmt.Sprintf("controller %q has a duplicate alias %q", name, alias))
   518→			}
   519→			aliases.Insert(alias)
   520→		}
   521→
   522→		controllers[name] = controllerDesc
   523→	}
   524→
   525→	// First add "special" controllers that aren't initialized normally. These controllers cannot be initialized
   526→	// in the main controller loop initialization, so we add them here only for the metadata and duplication detection.
   527→	// app.ControllerDescriptor#RequiresSpecialHandling should return true for such controllers
   528→	// The only known special case is the ServiceAccountTokenController which *must* be started
   529→	// first to ensure that the SA tokens for future controllers will exist. Think very carefully before adding new
   530→	// special controllers.
   531→	register(new
... (truncated)

   269→func (c *Controller) Run(ctx context.Context, workers int) {
   270→	defer utilruntime.HandleCrash()
   271→
   272→	// Start events processing pipeline.
   273→	c.eventBroadcaster.StartLogging(klog.Infof)
   274→	c.eventBroadcaster.StartRecordingToSink(&v1core.EventSinkImpl{Interface: c.client.CoreV1().Events("")})
   275→	defer c.eventBroadcaster.Shutdown()
   276→
   277→	defer c.serviceQueue.ShutDown()
   278→	defer c.topologyQueue.ShutDown()
   279→
   280→	logger := klog.FromContext(ctx)
   281→	logger.Info("Starting endpoint slice controller")
   282→	defer logger.Info("Shutting down endpoint slice controller")
   283→
   284→	if !cache.WaitForNamedCacheSync("endpoint_slice", ctx.Done(), c.podsSynced, c.servicesSynced, c.endpointSlicesSynced, c.nodesSynced) {
   285→		return
   286→	}
   287→
   288→	logger.V(2).Info("Starting service queue worker threads", "total", workers)
   289→	for i := 0; i < workers; i++ {
   290→		go wait.Until(func() { c.serviceQueueWorker(logger) }, c.workerLoopPeriod, ctx.Done())
   291→	}
   292→	logger.V(2).Info("Starting topology queue worker threads", "total", 1)
   293→	go wait.Until(func() { c.topologyQueueWorker(logger) }, c.workerLoopPeriod, ctx.Done())
   294→
   295→	<-ctx.Done()
   296→}
   297→
   298→// serviceQueueWorker runs a worker thread that just dequeues items, processes
   299→// them, and marks them done. You may run as many of these in parallel as you
   300→// wish; the workqueue guarantees that they will not end up processing the same
   301→// service at the same time
   302→func (c *Controller) serviceQueueWorker(logger klog.Logger) {
   303→	for c.processNextServiceWorkItem(logger) {
   304→	}
   305→}
   306→

   308→	cK

   162→func (c *Controller) Run(ctx context.Context, workers int) error {
   163→	defer utilruntime.HandleCrash()
   164→	defer c.workqueue.ShutDown()
   165→	logger := klog.FromContext(ctx)
   166→
   167→	// Start the informer factories to begin populating the informer caches
   168→	logger.Info("Starting Foo controller")
   169→
   170→	// Wait for the caches to be synced before starting workers
   171→	logger.Info("Waiting for informer caches to sync")
   172→
   173→	if ok := cache.WaitForCacheSync(ctx.Done(), c.deploymentsSynced, c.foosSynced); !ok {
   174→		return fmt.Errorf("failed to wait for caches to sync")
   175→	}
   176→
   177→	logger.Info("Starting workers", "count", workers)
   178→	// Launch two workers to process Foo resources
   179→	for i := 0; i < workers; i++ {
   180→		go wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, c.runWorker, time.Second)
   181→	}
   182→
   183→	logger.Info("Started workers")
   184→	<-ctx.Done()
   185→	logger.Info("Shutting down workers")
   186→
   187→	return nil
   188→}

160-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of how controllers register themselves in Kubernetes. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

**Important Discovery**: The Kubernetes codebase itself **does NOT use sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime**. Instead, it implements its own custom controller management system.

### Controller Registration Pattern in Kubernetes

1. **ControllerDescriptor** (`cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:495`) - Central registration mechanism containing:
   - Controller name and aliases
   - `initFunc` - function that creates and starts the controller
   - Feature gate requirements
   - Special handling flags

2. **ControllerContext** - Contains resources passed to each controller:
   - Kubernetes API clients
   - SharedInformerFactory for watching resources
   - RESTMapper, ResyncPeriod, etc.

3. **StartControllers** → **StartController** flow - Executes the controller's initFunc with the context

### Reconciliation Patterns (Non-Controller-Runtime)

**Work Queue Pattern** (used by sample controllers):
- Controllers implement `Run(ctx, workers)` 
- Use `workqueue.RateLimitingInterface` to queue work items
- Workers call `syncHandler()` for reconciliation logic
- Handles backoff/requeuing on errors

**Custom Reconciler Interfaces** (EndpointReconciler):
- Custom interface for API server endpoint reconciliation
- Methods like `ReconcileEndpoints()`, `RemoveEndpoints()`, `StopReconciling()`
- Implementations using instance counts or leases

The answer.json file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains all relevant file paths, symbols, and a detailed explanation of the controller registration and reconciliation chain.

This reconciles state for the attach/detach controller. That\n// reconciles state for the kubelet volume manager.\ntype Reconciler interface {\n\t// Starts running the reconciliation loop which executes periodically, checks\n\t// if volumes that should be attached are attached and volumes that should\n\t// be detached are detached. If during this time the volume\n// becomes used by a new pod, the detach request will be aborted and the timer\n// cleared.\nfunc NewReconciler(\n\tloopPeriod corelisters.NodeLister,\n\trecorder record.EventRecorder) Reconciler {\n\treturn &reconciler{\n\t\tloopPeriod:                  loopPeriod,\n\t\tmaxWaitForUnmountDuration:   maxWaitForUnmountDuration,\n\t\tsyncDuration:                syncDuration,\n\t\tdisableReconciliationSync:   disableReconciliationSync,\n\t\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout: time.Duration\n\tdesiredStateOfWorld         cache.DesiredStateOfWorld\n\tactualStateOfWorld          cache.ActualStateOfWorld\n\tattacherDetacher time.Time\n\tdisableReconciliationSync   bool\n\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout bool\n\trecorder                    record.EventRecorder\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n\twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, rc.reconciliationLoopFunc(ctx), rc.loopPeriod)\n}\n\n// reconciliationLoopFunc this can be disabled via cli option disableReconciliation.\n// It periodically checks whether the attached volumes from actual state\n// are still attached to the node and update the status if they are not.\nfunc (rc *reconciler) reconciliationLoopFunc(ctx context.Context) func(context.Context) {\n\treturn func(ctx context.Context) {\n\n\t\trc.reconcile(ctx)\n\t\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\t\tif rc.disableReconciliationSync {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Skipping reconciling attached volumes still attached since it is disabled via the command line\")\n\t\t} else if rc.syncDuration < time.Second {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Skipping reconciling attached volumes still attached since it is set to less than one second via the command line\")\n\t\t} else if time.Since(rc.timeOfLastSync) > rc.syncDuration {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Starting reconciling attached volumes still attached\")\n\t\t\trc.sync()\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) sync() {\n\tdefer rc.updateSyncTime()\n\trc.syncStates()\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) updateSyncTime() {\n\trc.timeOfLastSync = time.Now()\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) syncStates() {\n\tvolumesPerNode := rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachedVolumesPerNode()\n\trc.attacherDetacher.VerifyVolumesAreAttached(volumesPerNode, rc.actualStateOfWorld)\n}\n\n// hasOutOfServiceTaint returns true if the node has out-of-service taint present.\nfunc (rc *reconciler) hasOutOfServiceTaint(nodeName types.NodeName) (bool, error) {\n\tnode, err := rc.nodeLister.Get(string(nodeName))\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nodeIsHealthy(nodeName types.NodeName) (bool, error) {\n\tnode, err := rc.nodeLister.Get(string(nodeName))\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn false, err\n\t}\n\treturn nodeutil.IsNodeReady(node), nil\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) reconcile(ctx context.Context) {\n\t// Detaches are triggered before attaches so that volumes referenced by\n\t// pods that are rescheduled to a different node are detached first.\n\n\t// Ensure volumes that should be detached are detached.\n\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\tfor _, attachedVolume := range rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachedVolumes() {\n\t\tif !rc.desiredStateOfWorld.VolumeExists(\n\t\t\tattachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName) {\n\n\t\t\t// Check whether there already exist an operation pending, and don't even\n\t\t\t// try to operationexecutor.DetachOperationName) {\n\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running or still in exponential backoff for node. Can't start detach\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tif !rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationSafeToRetry(attachedVolume.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, \"\" /* nodeName */, operationexecutor.DetachOperationName) {\n\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running or still in exponential backoff in the cluster. Can't start detach for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Because the whether the umount drain timer expired\n\t\t\tmaxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired := elapsedTime > rc.maxWaitForUnmountDuration\n\n\t\t\tisHealthy, err := rc.nodeIsHealthy(attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to get health of node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Force detach volumes from unhealthy nodes after maxWaitForUnmountDuration if force detach is enabled\n\t\t\t// Ensure that the timeout condition checks this correctly so that the correct metric is updated below\n\t\t\tforceDetatchTimeoutExpired := maxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired && !rc.disableForceDetachOnTimeout\n\t\t\tif maxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired && rc.disableForceDetachOnTimeout {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Drain timeout expired for volume but disableForceDetachOnTimeout was set\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tforceDetach := !isHealthy && forceDetatchTimeoutExpired\n\n\t\t\thasOutOfServiceTaint, err := rc.hasOutOfServiceTaint(attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to get taint specs for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Check whether volume is still mounted. Skip detach if it is still mounted unless we have\n\t\t\t// decided to force detach or the node has `node.kubernetes.io/out-of-service` taint.\n\t\t\tif attachedVolume.MountedByNode && !forceDetach && !hasOutOfServiceTaint {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Cannot detach volume because it is still mounted\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Before triggering volume detach, mark volume as detached and update the node status\n\t\t\t// If it fails to update node status, skip detach volume\n\t\t\t// If volume detach operation fails, the volume needs to be added back to report as attached so that node status\n\t\t\t// has the correct volume attachment information.\n\t\t\terr = rc.actualStateOfWorld.RemoveVolumeFromReportAsAttached(attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"RemoveVolumeFromReportAsAttached failed while removing volume from node\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)),\n\t\t\t\t\t\"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName,\n\t\t\t\t\t\"err\", err)\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Update Node Status to indicate volume is no longer safe to mount.\n\t\t\terr = rc.nodeStatusUpdater.UpdateNodeStatusForNode(logger, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t// Skip detaching this volume if unable to update node status\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"UpdateNodeStatusForNode failed while attempting to report volume as attached\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t// Add volume back to ReportAsAttached if UpdateNodeStatusForNode call failed so that node status updater will add it back to VolumeAttached list.\n\t\t\t\t// It is needed here too because DetachVolume is not call actually and we keep the data consistency for every reconcile.\n\t\t\t\trc.actualStateOfWorld.AddVolumeToReportAsAttached(logger, attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Trigger detach volume which requires verifying safe to detach step\n\t\t\t// If forceDetatchTimeoutExpired is true, skip verifySafeToDetach check\n\t\t\t// If the node has node.kubernetes.io/out-of-service taint with NoExecute effect, skip verifySafeToDetach check\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Starting attacherDetacher.DetachVolume\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\tif hasOutOfServiceTaint {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"node has out-of-service taint\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tverifySafeToDetach := !(forceDetatchTimeoutExpired || attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t} else { // force detach\n\t\t\t\t\tif forceDetatchTimeoutExpired attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\trc.attachDesiredVolumes(logger)\n\n\t// Update Node Status\n\terr := rc.nodeStatusUpdater.UpdateNodeStatuses(logger)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"UpdateNodeStatuses failed\", \"err\", err)\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) attachDesiredVolumes(logger klog.Logger) {\n\t// Ensure volumes that should be attached are attached.\n\tfor _, volumeToAttach := range rc.desiredStateOfWorld.GetVolumesToAttach() {\n\t\tif util.IsMultiAttachAllowed(volumeToAttach.VolumeSpec) {\n\t\t\t// Don't even try to start an operation if there is already one running for the given volume and node.\n\t\t\tif rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationPending(volumeToAttach.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, volumeToAttach.NodeName) Can't start attach for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(volumeToAttach.NodeName)), \"volumeNames\", volumeToAttach.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Because the attach already attached to different node(s).\nfunc (rc *reconciler) reportMultiAttachError(logger klog.Logger, volumeToAttach cache.VolumeToAttach, nodes []types.NodeName) {\n\t// Filter out the current node from list of nodes where the volume is\n\t// attached.\n\t// Some methods need []string, some other needs []NodeName, collect both.\n\t// In theory, these arrays should have always only one The pod must have been deleted already.\n\t\tsimpleMsg, _ := volumeToAttach.GenerateMsg(\"Multi-Attach error\", \"Volume is already exclusively attached to one node and can't be attached to another\")\n\t\tfor _, pod := range volumeToAttach.ScheduledPods {\n\t\t\trc.recorder.Eventf(pod, v1.EventTypeWarning, kevents.FailedAttachVolume, simpleMsg)\n\t\t}\n\t\t// Log detailed message to system admin\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Multi-Attach error: volume is already exclusively attached and can't be attached to another node\", \"attachedTo\", otherNodesStr, \"volume\", volumeToAttach)\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// There are pods that require the volume and run on another node. Typically\n\t// it's user error, e.g. a ReplicaSet uses a PVC and has >1 replicas. Let\n\t// the user know what pods are blocking the volume.\n\tfor _, scheduledPod := range volumeToAttach.ScheduledPods {\n\t\t// Each scheduledPod must get a custom message. They can run in\n\t\t// different namespaces and user of a namespace should not see names of\n\t\t// pods in other namespaces.\n\t\tlocalPodNames := []string{} // Names of pods in scheduledPods's namespace\n\t\totherPods := 0              // Count of pods in other namespaces\n\t\tfor _, pod := range pods {\n\t\t\tif pod.Namespace == scheduledPod.Namespace {\n\t\t\t\tlocalPodNames = append(localPodNames, pod.Name)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\totherPods++\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tvar msg string\n\t\tif len(localPodNames) > 0 {\n\t\t\tmsg = fmt.Sprintf(\"Volume is already used by pod(s) %s\", strings.Join(localPodNames, \", \"))\n\t\t\tif otherPods > 0 {\n\t\t\t\tmsg = fmt.Sprintf(\"%s and %d pod(s) in different namespaces\", msg, otherPods)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t// No local pods, there are pods only in different namespaces.\n\t\t\tmsg = fmt.Sprintf(\"Volume is already used by %d pod(s) in different namespaces\", otherPods)\n\t\t}\n\t\tsimpleMsg, _ := volumeToAttach.GenerateMsg(\"Multi-Attach error\", msg)\n\t\trc.recorder.Eventf(scheduledPod, v1.EventTypeWarning, kevents.FailedAttachVolume, simpleMsg)\n\t}\n\n\t// Log all pods for system admin\n\tlogger.Info(\"Multi-Attach error: volume is already used by pods\", \"pods\", klog.KObjSlice(pods), \"attachedTo\", otherNodesStr, \"volume\", volumeToAttach)\n}\n",

94\u2192\t// for further adjustment\n    95\u2192\tfor _, existingSlice := range existingSlices {\n    96\u2192\t\t// service no longer supports that address type, add it to deleted slices\n    97\u2192\t\tif !serviceSupportedAddressesTypes.Has(existingSlice.AddressType) {\n    98\u2192\t\t\tif r.topologyCache != nil {\n    99\u2192\t\t\t\tsvcKey, err := ServiceControllerKey(existingSlice)\n   100\u2192\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   101\u2192\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Couldn't get key to remove EndpointSlice from topology cache\", \"existingSlice\", existingSlice, \"err\", err)\n   102\u2192\t\t\t\t} else {\n   103\u2192\t\t\t\t\tr.topologyCache.RemoveHints(svcKey, existingSlice.AddressType)\n   104\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   105\u2192\t\t\t}\n   106\u2192\n   107\u2192\t\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete, existingSlice)\n   108\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   109\u2192\t\t}\n   110\u2192\n   111\u2192\t\t// add list if it is not on our map\n   112\u2192\t\tif _, ok := slicesByAddressType[existingSlice.AddressType]; !ok {\n   113\u2192\t\t\tslicesByAddressType[existingSlice.AddressType] = make([]*discovery.EndpointSlice, 0, 1)\n   114\u2192\t\t}\n   115\u2192\n   116\u2192\t\tslicesByAddressType[existingSlice.AddressType] = append(slicesByAddressType[existingSlice.AddressType], existingSlice)\n   117\u2192\t}\n   118\u2192\n   119\u2192\t// reconcile for existing.\n   120\u2192\tfor addressType := range serviceSupportedAddressesTypes {\n   121\u2192\t\texistingSlices := slicesByAddressType[addressType]\n   122\u2192\t\terr 126\u2192\t}\n   127\u2192\n   128\u2192\t// delete those which are of addressType that is no longer supported\n   129\u2192\t// by the service\n   130\u2192\tfor _, sliceToDelete := range 135\u2192\t\t\tr.endpointSliceTracker.ExpectDeletion(sliceToDelete)\n   136\u2192\t\t\tmetrics.EndpointSliceChanges.WithLabelValues(\"delete\").Inc()\n   137\u2192\t\t}\n   138\u2192\t}\n   139\u2192\n   140\u2192\treturn utilerrors.NewAggregate(errs)\n   141\u2192}\n   142\u2192\n   143\u2192// reconcileByAddressType takes a set of pods currently matching a service selector and\n   144\u2192// compares them with the endpoints already present in any existing endpoint\n   145\u2192// slices (by address type) for the given service. It creates, updates, or deletes endpoint slices\n   146\u2192// to ensure the desired set of pods are represented by endpoint slices.\n   147\u2192func (r *Reconciler) reconcileByAddressType(logger will remove the Pod, but we want to avoid\n   198\u2192\t\t\t// situations where a reference from a Pod to a missing node can leave the EndpointSlice\n   199\u2192\t\t\t// stuck forever.\n   200\u2192\t\t\t// On the other side, if the service.Spec.PublishNotReadyAddresses is set we just add the\n   201\u2192\t\t\t// Pod, since the user is explicitly indicating that the Pod address should service.Namespace, service.Name, pod.Spec.NodeName))\n   205\u2192\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   206\u2192\t\t\t}\n   207\u2192\t\t}\n   208\u2192\t\tendpoint := podToEndpoint(pod, node, service, addressType)\n 219\u2192\tfor portMap, desiredEndpoints := range desiredEndpointsByPortMap {\n   220\u2192\t\tnumEndpoints := len(desiredEndpoints)\n   221\u2192\t\tpmSlicesToCreate, pmSlicesToUpdate, 224\u2192\t\ttotalAdded += added\n   225\u2192\t\ttotalRemoved += removed\n   226\u2192\n   227\u2192\t\tspMetrics.Set(portMap, metrics.EfficiencyInfo{\n   228\u2192\t\t\tEndpoints: numEndpoints,\n   229\u2192\t\t\tSlices:    len(existingSlicesByPortMap[portMap]) + len(pmSlicesToCreate) - len(pmSlicesToDelete),\n   230\u2192\t\t})\n   231\u2192\n   232\u2192\t\tslicesToCreate = 246\u2192\tif len(existingSlices) == len(slicesToDelete) && len(slicesToCreate) < 1 {\n   247\u2192\t\t// Check for existing placeholder slice outside of the core control flow\n   248\u2192\t\tplaceholderSlice := newEndpointSlice(logger, service, &endpointMeta{ports: []discovery.EndpointPort{}, addressType: addressType}, r.controllerName)\n   249\u2192\t\tif len(slicesToDelete) == 1 && placeholderSliceCompare.DeepEqual(slicesToDelete[0], placeholderSlice) {\n   250\u2192\t\t\t// We are about to unnecessarily delete/recreate the placeholder, remove it now.\n   251\u2192\t\t\tslicesToDelete = slicesToDelete[:0]\n   252\u2192\t\t} else {\n   253\u2192\t\t\tslicesToCreate = append(slicesToCreate, placeholderSlice)\n   254\u2192\t\t}\n   255\u2192\t\tspMetrics.Set(endpointsliceutil.NewPortMapKey(placeholderSlice.Ports), metrics.EfficiencyInfo{\n   256\u2192\t\t\tEndpoints: 0,\n   257\u2192\t\t\tSlices:    1,\n   258\u2192\t\t})\n   259\u2192\t}\n   260\u2192\n   261\u2192\tmetrics.EndpointsAddedPerSync.WithLabelValues().Observe(float64(totalAdded))\n   262\u2192\tmetrics.EndpointsRemovedPerSync.WithLabelValues().Observe(float64(totalRemoved))\n   263\u2192\n   264\u2192\tserviceNN := types.NamespacedName{Name: service.Name, Namespace: service.Namespace}\n   265\u2192\tr.metricsCache.UpdateServicePortCache(serviceNN, spMetrics)\n   266\u2192\n   267\u2192\t// Topology hints are assigned per address type. This means it is\n   268\u2192\t// theoretically possible for endpoints of one address type to be assigned\n   269\u2192\t// hints while another endpoints of another address type are not.\n   270\u2192\tsi := &topologycache.SliceInfo{\n   271\u2192\t\tServiceKey:  fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s\", service.Namespace, service.Name),\n   272\u2192\t\tAddressType: addressType,\n   273\u2192\t\tToCreate:    slicesToCreate,\n   274\u2192\t\tToUpdate:    slicesToUpdate,\n   275\u2192\t\tUnchanged:   unchangedSlices(existingSlices, slicesToUpdate, slicesToDelete),\n   276\u2192\t}\n   277\u2192\n   278\u2192\tcanUseTrafficDistribution := r.trafficDistributionEnabled && !hintsEnabled(service.Annotations)\n   279\u2192\n   280\u2192\t// Check if we need to add/remove hints based on the topology annotation.\n   281\u2192\t//\n   282\u2192\t// This if/else clause can be removed once the annotation has been deprecated.\n   283\u2192\t// Ref: https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/tree/master/keps/sig-network/4444-service-routing-preference\n   284\u2192\tif r.topologyCache != nil && hintsEnabled(service.Annotations) {\n   285\u2192\t\t// Reaching this point means that we need to configure hints based on the\n   286\u2192\t\t// topology annotation.\n   287\u2192\t\tslicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate, events = r.topologyCache.AddHints(logger, si)\n   288\u2192\n   289\u2192\t} else {\n   290\u2192\t\t// Reaching this point means that we will not be configuring hints based on\n   291\u2192\t\t// the topology annotation. We need to do 2 things:\n   292\u2192\t\t//  1. If hints were added previously based on the annotation, we need to\n   293\u2192\t\t//     clear up any locally cached hints from the topologyCache object.\n   294\u2192\t\t//  2. In other\n   296\u2192\t\t//     words, if we know that the `trafficDistribution` field has been\n   297\u2192\t\t//     correctly configured by the customer, we DO NOT remove the hints and\n   298\u2192\t\t//     wait for the trafficDist handlers to correctly configure them. Always\n   299\u2192\t\t//     unconditionally removing hints here (and letting them get readded by\n   300\u2192\t\t//     the trafficDist) adds extra overhead in the form of DeepCopy (done\n   301\u2192\t\t//     within topologyCache.RemoveHints)\n   302\u2192\n   303\u2192\t\t// Check 1.\n   304\u2192\t\tif r.topologyCache != nil {\n   305\u2192\t\t\tif 326\u2192\t\tr.metricsCache.UpdateTrafficDistributionForService(serviceNN, nil)\n   327\u2192\t}\n   328\u2192\n   329\u2192\terr := r.finalize(service, slicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate, slicesToDelete, triggerTime)\n   330\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   331\u2192\t\terrs = append(errs, err)\n   332\u2192\t}\n   333\u2192\tfor _, event := range events {\n   334\u2192\t\tr.eventRecorder.Event(service, event.EventType, event.Reason, event.Message)\n   335\u2192\t}\n   336\u2192\treturn utilerrors.NewAggregate(errs)\n   337\u2192\n   338\u2192}\n   339\u2192\n   340\u2192func NewReconciler(client clientset.Interface, nodeLister corelisters.NodeLister, maxEndpointsPerSlice int32, endpointSliceTracker *endpointsliceutil.EndpointSliceTracker, topologyCache *topologycache.TopologyCache, eventRecorder record.EventRecorder, controllerName string, options ...ReconcilerOption) *Reconciler {\n   341\u2192\tr := &Reconciler{\n   342\u2192\t\tclient:               client,\n   343\u2192\t\tnodeLister:           nodeLister,\n   344\u2192\t\tmaxEndpointsPerSlice: maxEndpointsPerSlice,\n   345\u2192\t\tendpointSliceTracker: endpointSliceTracker,\n   346\u2192\t\tmetricsCache:         metrics.NewCache(maxEndpointsPerSlice),\n   347\u2192\t\ttopologyCache:        topologyCache,\n   348\u2192\t\teventRecorder:        eventRecorder,\n   349\u2192\t\tcontrollerName:       controllerName,\n   350\u2192\t}\n   351\u2192\tfor _, option := range options {\n   352\u2192\t\toption(r)\n   353\u2192\t}\n   354\u2192\treturn r\n   355\u2192}\n   356\u2192\n   357\u2192// placeholderSliceCompare is a conversion func for comparing two placeholder endpoint slices.\n   358\u2192// It only compares the specific fields we care about.\n   359\u2192var placeholderSliceCompare = conversion.EqualitiesOrDie(\n   360\u2192\tfunc(a, b metav1.OwnerReference) bool {\n   361\u2192\t\treturn a.String() == b.String()\n   362\u2192\t},\n   363\u2192\tfunc(a, b metav1.ObjectMeta) bool {\n   364\u2192\t\tif a.Namespace != b.Namespace {\n   365\u2192\t\t\treturn false\n   366\u2192\t\t}\n   367\u2192\t\tfor k, v := range a.Labels {\n   368\u2192\t\t\tif b.Labels[k] != v {\n   369\u2192\t\t\t\treturn false\n   370\u2192\t\t\t}\n   371\u2192\t\t}\n   372\u2192\t\tfor k, v := range b.Labels {\n   373\u2192\t\t\tif a.Labels[k] != v {\n   374\u2192\t\t\t\treturn false\n   375\u2192\t\t\t}\n   376\u2192\t\t}\n   377\u2192\t\treturn true\n   378\u2192\t},\n   379\u2192)\n   380\u2192\n   381\u2192// finalize creates, updates, and deletes slices as specified\n   382\u2192func (r *Reconciler) finalize(\n   383\u2192\tservice *corev1.Service,\n   384\u2192\tslicesToCreate,\n   385\u2192\tslicesToUpdate,\n   386\u2192\tslicesToDelete []*discovery.EndpointSlice,\n   387\u2192\ttriggerTime time.Time,\n   388\u2192) error {\n   389\u2192\t// If there are slices to create and delete, change the creates to updates\n   390\u2192\t// of the slices that would otherwise be deleted.\n   391\u2192\tfor i := 0; i < len(slicesToDelete); {\n   392\u2192\t\tif len(slicesToCreate) == 0 {\n   393\u2192\t\t\tbreak\n   394\u2192\t\t}\n   395\u2192\t\tsliceToDelete := slicesToDelete[i]\n   396\u2192\t\tslice := slicesToCreate[len(slicesToCreate)-1]\n   397\u2192\t\t// Only update EndpointSlices that are owned by this Service and have\n   398\u2192\t\t// the same AddressType. We need to avoid updating EndpointSlices that\n   399\u2192\t\t// are being garbage collected for an old Service with the same name.\n   400\u2192\t\t// The AddressType field is immutable. Since Services also consider\n   401\u2192\t\t// IPFamily immutable, the only case where this should matter will be\n   402\u2192\t\t// the migration from IP to IPv4 and IPv6 AddressTypes, where there's a\n   403\u2192\t\t// chance EndpointSlices with an IP AddressType would otherwise be\n   404\u2192\t\t// updated to IPv4 or IPv6 without this check.\n   405\u2192\t\tif sliceToDelete.AddressType == slice.AddressType && ownedBy(sliceToDelete, service) {\n   406\u2192\t\t\tslice.Name = sliceToDelete.Name\n   407\u2192\t\t\tslicesToCreate = slicesToCreate[:len(slicesToCreate)-1]\n   408\u2192\t\t\tslicesToUpdate = append(slicesToUpdate, slice)\n   409\u2192\t\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete[:i], slicesToDelete[i+1:]...)\n   410\u2192\t\t} else {\n   411\u2192\t\t\ti++\n   412\u2192\t\t}\n   413\u2192\t}\n   414\u2192\n   415\u2192\t// Don't create new EndpointSlices if the Service is pending deletion. This\n   416\u2192\t// is to avoid a potential race condition with the garbage collector where\n   417\u2192\t// it tries to delete EndpointSlices as this controller replaces them.\n   418\u2192\tif service.DeletionTimestamp == nil {\n   419\u2192\t\tfor _, endpointSlice := range slicesToCreate {\n   420\u2192\t\t\taddTriggerTimeAnnotation(endpointSlice, triggerTime)\n   421\u2192\t\t\tcreatedSlice, err := r.client.DiscoveryV1().EndpointSlices(service.Namespace).Create(context.TODO(), endpointSlice, metav1.CreateOptions{})\n   422\u2192\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   423\u2192\t\t\t\t// If the namespace is terminating, creates will continue to fail. Simply drop the item.\n   424\u2192\t\t\t\tif errors.HasStatusCause(err, corev1.NamespaceTerminatingCause) {\n   425\u2192\t\t\t\t\treturn nil\n   426\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   427\u2192\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to create EndpointSlice for Service %s/%s: %v\", service.Namespace, service.Name, err)\n   428\u2192\t\t\t}\n   429\u2192\t\t\tr.endpointSliceTracker.Update(createdSlice)\n   430\u2192\t\t\tmetrics.EndpointSliceChanges.WithLabelValues(\"create\").Inc()\n   431\u2192\t\t}\n   432\u2192\t}\n   433\u2192\n   434\u2192\tfor _, endpointSlice := range slicesToUpdate {\n   435\u2192\t\taddTriggerTimeAnnotation(endpointSlice, triggerTime)\n   436\u2192\t\tupdatedSlice, err := r.client.DiscoveryV1().EndpointSlices(service.Namespace).Update(context.TODO(), endpointSlice, metav1.UpdateOptions{})\n   437\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   438\u2192\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to update %s EndpointSlice for Service %s/%s: %v\", endpointSlice.Name, service.Namespace, service.Name, err)\n   439\u2192\t\t}\n   440\u2192\t\tr.endpointSliceTracker.Update(updatedSlice)\n   441\u2192\t\tmetrics.EndpointSliceChanges.WithLabelValues(\"update\").Inc()\n   442\u2192\t}\n   443\u2192\n   444\u2192\tfor _, endpointSlice := range slicesToDelete {\n   445\u2192\t\terr := r.client.DiscoveryV1().EndpointSlices(service.Namespace).Delete(context.TODO(), endpointSlice.Name, 472\u2192// and delete. Here is how controllers register and reconcile in kubernetes/kubernetes:\\n\\n## Controller Registration Pattern\\n\\nControllers are registered through the ControllerDescriptor system defined in cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:\\n\\n1. **NewControllerDescriptors()** (line 495) - Registers all known controllers. Each controller descriptor contains:\\n   - A unique name (e.g., 'endpointslice-controller')\\n   - An initFunc that initializes the controller\\n   - Optional aliases\\n   - Feature gate requirements\\n\\n2. **ControllerDescriptor** - registration happens through ControllerDescriptor\\n\\nThe actual controller-runtime library (sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime) is only mentioned in a test comment (test/integration/cloudprovider/ccm_test.go:304) and is not used in the core Kubernetes codebase. Projects like kubebuilder use controller-runtime for custom controllers, but Kubernetes itself uses its own control loop implementation.\"\n}\n",

Instead, it uses a custom controller management pattern based on work queues and informers. Here is how controllers register and reconcile in kubernetes/kubernetes:\\n\\n## Controller Registration Pattern\\n\\nControllers are registered through the ControllerDescriptor system defined in cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:\\n\\n1. **NewControllerDescriptors()** (line 495) - Registers all known controllers. Each controller descriptor contains:\\n   - A unique name (e.g., 'endpointslice-controller')\\n   - An initFunc that initializes the controller\\n   - Optional aliases\\n   - Feature gate requirements\\n\\n2. **ControllerDescriptor** - Contains:\\n   - name: string\\n   - aliases: []string  \\n   - initFunc: function that creates and starts the controller\\n   - requiresSpecialHandling: bool (for controllers like ServiceAccountTokenController that must start first)\\n\\n3. **ControllerContext** (line 366) - Passed to each controller's initFunc containing:\\n   - ClientBuilder: for creating API clients\\n   - InformerFactory: SharedInformerFactory for watching resources\\n   - ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory: for metadata access\\n   - RESTMapper: for resource mapping\\n   - ResyncPeriod: function generating sync intervals\\n\\n## Controller Startup Flow\\n\\n1. **StartControllers()** (line 662) - Main function that starts all registered controllers\\n2. **StartController()** (line 710) - Starts an individual controller by:\\n   - Checking feature gate requirements\\n   - Calling the controller's initFunc\\n   - Starting worker goroutines\\n\\n## Reconciliation Pattern (Non-Controller-Runtime)\\n\\nInstead of the controller-runtime Reconciler interface, Kubernetes uses:\\n\\n### Work Queue Pattern (Standard)\\nSeen in staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go:\\n- Controller struct with:\\n  - workqueue.RateLimitingInterface for queuing work items\\n  - Informer synced callbacks for coordinating startup\\n  - Event recorder for recording cluster events\\n\\n- Run(ctx, workers) - Main loop that:\\n  - Waits for informer caches to sync (WaitForCacheSync)\\n  - Launches N worker goroutines\\n  - Each worker calls runWorker -> processNextWorkItem -> syncHandler\\n\\n- syncHandler(ctx, objectRef) - The reconciliation logic that:\\n  - Gets the object from lister\\n  - Compares desired vs actual state\\n  - Performs operations to converge state\\n  - Handles errors with backoff/requeuing\\n\\n### Endpoint Reconciler Pattern (Custom)\\nSeen in pkg/controlplane/reconcilers/reconcilers.go:\\n- EndpointReconciler interface with methods:\\n  - ReconcileEndpoints() - Reconciles master endpoints\\n  - RemoveEndpoints() - Removes endpoint entries\\n  - StopReconciling() - Cleanly stops reconciliation\\n  - Destroy() - Cleans up resources\\n\\n- Implementations:\\n  - masterCountEndpointReconciler (instancecount.go) - Reconciles based on expected master count\\n  - leaseEndpointReconciler (lease.go) - Stores endpoint info using leases\\n\\n### Apiserver Reconciler Pattern\\nSeen in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/reconcilers/peer_endpoint_lease.go:\\n- PeerEndpointLeaseReconciler interface for managing apiserver peer endpoints\\n- PeerEndpointLeaseController struct with:\\n  - Run(stopCh) - Main reconciliation loop\\n  - UpdatePeerEndpointLeases() - Periodic reconciliation function\\n  - Fixed interval polling (not event-driven)\\n\\n## Key Differences from Controller-Runtime\\n\\n1. **No Manager**: Controllers are started directly, not registered with a manager\\n2. **No Reconcile Interface**: Controllers implement custom Run/sync methods, not Reconcile(ctx, Request) (Result, error)\\n3. **Work Queue Based**: Uses client-go's workqueue.RateLimitingInterface, not controller-runtime's reconcile.Request/Result\\n4. **Manual Startup**: Controllers initialize event handlers and workers directly via cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs\\n5. **No SetupWithManager**: Controllers don't have a SetupWithManager method - registration happens through ControllerDescriptor\\n\\nThe actual controller-runtime library (sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime) is only mentioned in a test comment (test/integration/cloudprovider/ccm_test.go:304) and is not used in the core Kubernetes codebase. Projects like kubebuilder use controller-runtime for custom controllers, but Kubernetes itself uses its own control loop implementation.\"\n}\n",
